Rulings on Foundling and Lineage Claims
Explains rulings on foundling custody and lineage claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rulings on foundling lineage, distinguish between the intra-Hanafi positions on multiple claimants, and apply the principle of istihsan to validate a finder's claim.

Core Idea
A foundling's lineage can be established from the finder by istihsan, and multiple claimants are all accepted per Abu Hanifa, but limited by his disciples.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains the rules for foundlings (luqata) – children found abandoned. It focuses on who can claim the child's lineage and under what conditions. The text resolves apparent contradictions by using istihsan, a distinctive Hanafi method, and presents an intra-madhhab disagreement among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding multiple claimants. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for applying the correct ruling in custody and lineage cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary rules of custody and lineage
The finder has the prior right to keep the foundling; no one may take it forcibly. Lineage claims are valid from any claimant, including the finder, by istihsan despite the apparent contradiction.
The finder's claim is accepted because he undertakes maintenance, and contradiction does not prevent nasab.
2
Understand the role of bodily marks in competing claims
If two or more claim the child, the one who can describe a distinctive mark on the child's body (not on clothing) and is truthful gains exclusive lineage.
If no mark or both describe, they are equal, and the finder's prior custody gives him preference.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on number of claimants
Abu Hanifa: any number of claimants equally establish lineage. Abu Yusuf: maximum two. Muhammad: maximum three. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's view.
The difference stems from analogy vs. social practicality.
4
Examine rules for slave and dhimmi claimants
If a slave claims the foundling, the child becomes free (presumption of freedom). If a dhimmi claims, the child's religion follows the place of finding: Muslim if found in Muslim territory, dhimmi if in dhimmi territory.
There is a narration difference when the finder's religion differs from the place.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its practical application
The preferred position is that the finder is most entitled; for multiple claimants, Abu Hanifa's unlimited view is adopted. The child's religion is determined by the finder's religion if no contradictory evidence.
This ensures the child's best interest (maslaha).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب اللقيط تعريفه وأحكامه
٥١٣
ولا يؤخذ من آخذه. ونسبه ممن ادعاه، ولو رجلين، أو ممن يصف منهما علامةً به ، أو عبداً، وكان حراً
(1) ولا يؤخذ من آخذه. ونسبه ممن ادعاه، ولو رجلين ، أو ممن يصفُ منهما علامة به : أي لو ادعى رجلان نسبه ، فإن وَصَفَ أحدهما علامة في جسده، وكان في ذلك صادقا، فالنسب منه ، وإلا فهما سواء . ثمَّ عطف على قوله : ولو رجلين ؛ قوله : (أو عبداً، وكان حراً)
[١] قوله : ولا يؤخذ ؛ يعني ليس بغير الملتقط أن يأخذ اللقيط منه جبراً ؛ لثبوتِ حق الحفظ له لسبق يده. [٢] قوله : ممن ادّعاه ؛ سواء كان ملتقطاً أو غيره، والقياس أن لا يصح نسبه من الملتقط ؛ لأنه زعم أنه في يده لقيط، فدعواه أنه ابنه تكون متناقضة، وفي الاستحسان يصح؛ لأنه يلتزم حفظه ونفقته بهذا الإقرار والتناقض لا يمنع دعوى النسب. كذا في حواشي «الهداية».
[٣] قوله : ولو رجلين ؛ إذا لم يوجد لأحدهما مرجّح ، لما لو ادّعى نسبه . وآخر معه، يكون الملتقط أولى ؛ لأنّ صاحب اليد أولى، وحكم ما زاد على مدعيين كذلك عند أبي حنيفة له ، وعند محمد الله يثبت من الثلاث لا الأكثر، وعند أبي يوسف لا يثبت لأكثر من اثنين.
[٤] قوله : به ؛ أي بجسده لا بثوبه ؛ لأنّ الثَّوبَ غير ملازم له ، كذا في «النهر». [٥] قوله : وإلا ؛ أي وإن لم يصف أحد منهما علامة ، أو وصف وكذبه الحس. [٦] قوله : فهما سواء ؛ إلا إذا كانت دعوى أحدهما سابقة على دعوى الآخر، أو ثبتت دعوى أحدهما بحجّة دون له لآخر، أو شهد بهما سن الطفل، وخالف دعوى الآخر، فحينئذ يثبتُ النّسب من واحد.
[٧] قوله : لأن الأصل؛ يعني الأصل في دار الإسلام الحرية، والرقُ إنما يثبتُ بعارض. فإن قلت : ابنُ العبدِ كيف يكون حراً؟ قلت: لا استحالة فيه، فإنّ العبد قد تلد له الأمة، وقد تلد له الحرّة، وحينئذ لا يكون عبداً.
[٨] قوله : أو ذمياً؛ أي إن كان مدّعي النسب ذمياً يثبت نسبه منه، لكن اللقيط يصير مسلماً تبعاً للدار إذا وجد في مصر من أمصار المسلمين، أو في قرية من قراهم وهذا استحسان؛ لأنّ دعواه تضمّنت النسب، وهو نافع للصغير، وإبطال الإسلام الثابت بالدار وهو مضرّ له، فصحت دعوته فيما ينفعه دون ما يضره.
[٩] قوله : وقد وجد.. الخ؛ قال في «الهداية»: إن وجد في قرية من قرى أهل الذمة أو في بيعة أو كنيسة كان ذمياً، وهذا الجواب فيما إذا كان الواحد ذمياً رواية واحدة. وإن كان الواجد مسلماً في هذا المكان أو ذمياً في مكان المسلمين، اختلفت الرواية فيه: ففي «كتاب اللقيط» اعتبر المكان لسبقه، وفي «كتاب الدعوى»: في بعض النسخ اعتبر الواجد، وهو رواية ابن سماعة عن محمد الله؛ لقوة اليد، وفي بعض النسخ: اعتبر الإسلام بظاهر الصغير.
Book of the Foundling: its definition and rulings. 513. And it is not taken from its taker. And his lineage is from whoever claims him, even if two men, or from whoever describes from them a mark on him, or a slave, and he is free. (1) And it is not taken from its taker. And his lineage is from whoever claims him, even if two men, or from whoever describes from them a mark on him: meaning if two men claim his lineage, and one describes a mark on his body and is truthful in that, then lineage is from him; otherwise they are equal. Then he coordinated with his statement: 'and even if two men'; his statement: 'or a slave, and he is free'. [1] His statement: 'and it is not taken'; meaning no one other than the finder may take the foundling from him forcibly, because the right of custody is established for him due to his prior possession. [2] His statement: 'from whoever claims him'; whether he is the finder or someone else. By analogy, his lineage is not valid from the finder because he claims it is a foundling in his hand, so his claim that it is his son is contradictory; but by istihsan it is valid, because he undertakes its custody and maintenance by this acknowledgment, and contradiction does not prevent claiming lineage. Thus in the glosses of al-Hidayah. [3] His statement: 'even if two men'; when there is no preponderance for either, because if one claims his lineage and another is with him, the finder is more entitled because the one in possession is more entitled. The ruling for more than two claimants is similar according to Abu Hanifa. According to Muhammad, it is established from three but not more. According to Abu Yusuf, it is not established for more than two. [4] His statement: 'on him'; meaning on his body, not on his garment, because the garment is not inherent to him. Thus in al-Nahr. [5] His statement: 'otherwise'; meaning if neither describes a mark, or describes and the senses belie him. [6] His statement: 'they are equal'; except if one's claim precedes the other's, or one's claim is established by evidence while the other's is not, or the child's age points to one and contradicts the other; then lineage is established from one. [7] His statement: 'because the principle'; meaning the principle in the abode of Islam is freedom; slavery is only established by an accident. If you say: how can a slave's child be free? I say: there is no impossibility, for a slave may have a child from a slave woman and from a free woman, in which case he is not a slave. [8] His statement: 'or a dhimmi'; meaning if the claimant of lineage is a dhimmi, his lineage is established from him, but the foundling becomes Muslim following the abode if found in a city of Muslim cities or in a village of their villages. This is istihsan, because his claim includes lineage, which benefits the minor, and voiding Islam established by the abode is harmful to him. So his claim is valid in what benefits him but not in what harms him. [9] His statement: 'and if found... etc.'; al-Hidayah said: if found in a village of dhimmi villages or in a church or synagogue, he is a dhimmi. This answer is one narration when the finder is a dhimmi. If the finder is a Muslim in that place or a dhimmi in a Muslim place, the narration varies: in Kitab al-Luqata the place is considered due to its precedence; in Kitab al-Da'wa in some copies the finder is considered, which is the narration of Ibn Sama'a from Muhammad due to the strength of possession; and in some copies Islam is considered by the apparent condition of the child.
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This passage deals with the rulings on foundlings (al-luqata), specifically the child found abandoned. It establishes the principle that the finder has a right to keep the foundling and no one may forcibly take it from him. Regarding lineage: if someone claims the foundling as his child, the claim is valid provided it is not contradicted. A finder’s own claim is considered valid by istihsan despite the apparent contradiction (he initially treated it as a foundling), because he undertakes its care. When two people claim the child and only one describes a distinctive bodily mark, that one’s claim prevails; if both describe a mark or neither, and no other preponderance exists, they are equal and the finder retains the child. For more than two claimants, Abu Hanifa holds that the ruling for two extends to any number, but Abu Yusuf limits it to two, and Muhammad limits it to three. The child is presumed free (not a slave) in a Muslim land. If the claimant is a slave, the child becomes free because the child’s origin is freedom. If the claimant is a dhimmi and the child is found in Muslim territory, the child remains Muslim; if found in dhimmi territory, the child becomes dhimmi. There is also a transmission difference regarding the case when the finder’s religion differs from the place.

Key Terms
لقيط (laqīṭ): A foundling, a child found abandoned and taken in by someone.
ملتقط (multaqiṭ): The person who finds and takes custody of the foundling.
نسب (nasab): Lineage; the legal relationship of parentage.
علامة (ʿalāmah): A distinctive physical mark on the child's body.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juridical preference; departing from strict analogy for a more equitable ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if two men claim a foundling and one describes a bodily mark that is true, what determines the lineage?
A) Both are equal and the finder keeps the child.
B) The one who described the mark becomes the father.
C) The child chooses which one to follow.
D) The case is referred to a judge for decision.

Key Takeaway
The finder's claim of lineage is accepted by istihsan; in multi-claimant disputes, Abu Hanifa's permissive view is relied upon, subject to the condition of a bodily mark or the finder's priority.
